commit c900ecc9b09c0de27e1f15f50ad77115fc0ef0cb
Author: alyssawangqq <alyssawangqq@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon May 31 02:51:30 2021 -0400

    Fixing bug when python has multiple line for function declaration due to formatting (#319)
    
    * Fixing bug when python has multiple line for function declaration due to formatting
    
    Currently there's bug in python Lizard when getting LOC and CCN when func declaration has multiple lines. It will only count the function declaration lines but not the implementation. This is because the original code uses indentation to check function ending while for multi-line declaration, the last line will start with ")" with no indent.
    
    Example:
    ```
    def f1(a,
        b
    ):
      # function implementation for 10 lines
    ```
    
    Issue in https://github.com/terryyin/lizard/issues/292
    
    * Add unit test for pull request #319
    
    * Fix testPython.py

A	.DS_Store
M	lizard_languages/python.py
A	test/.DS_Store
M	test/test_languages/testPython.py

commit b1548409d3ada00d1d6d7280e5ae47d7820f74f3
Author: Corentin Plouet <corentin@plouet.name>
Date:   Fri Aug 23 03:40:53 2019 +1000

    Get rid of MD5 comparison in test + use compatible codec.
    
    * The MD5 comparison is too fragile and hard to maintain
      (since it would require recomputing whenever the output
      changes). It makes more sense to simply compare the
      first line to ensure we have the right output type.
    * Using the codecs library works with Python 2 and 3.

commit e1011cd28f36fd6ae1fd297c654e0c026318f1a0
Author: Corentin Plouet <corentin@plouet.name>
Date:   Fri Aug 23 02:20:49 2019 +1000

    Added a command-line option -o / --output_file.
    
    It does what the name implies.
    If the output format is not otherwise specified, it also tries to
    infer it from the file name (i.e. "--output_file complexity.html"
    will indeed generate a HTML file).
    
    + added two test cases (8 distinct tests in total)
    + renamed class TestFileOutput -> TestFileInformationOutput, to
      reduce confusion.

commit 0e797eeeb72b5ab4fe4770bd4738f03f510c30fa
Author: Corentin Plouet <corentin@plouet.name>
Date:   Thu Aug 22 22:00:47 2019 +1000

    Fixed warning threshold inconsistency in HTML output.
    
    As documented, warnings are generated when metrics (e.g. CCN) are
    bigger (>) than the threshold. Thus, we should use the same logic
    in the HTML output, and use greater (>) instead of gte (>=).

    fix regular expression test case
    ==================
    the old regex may make some mistake like this, so i change the regex to fix that:
    
    code:
    if (a / b < 5){
       // do something
    }
    
    token:
    if,
    (,
    a,
    / b < 5){
       /,
    /,
    do something,
    }

commit 12fad78de01aab46f66d0c66e01f19fffa9fd3dd
Merge: 71478c5 fd44240
Author: Terry Yin <terry.yinzhe@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Jan 2 09:40:09 2017 +0800

    Merge pull request #174 from rakhimov/braceless-consecutive-structures
    
    Fix handling of braceless consecutive NS structures

commit fd44240fa4f4e7eccc36eb4a2dd76687479e5010
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Dec 30 13:24:05 2016 -0800

    Implement proper NS for paired structures
    
    Paired structures: try-catch, catch-catch, if-else, do-while.
    These structures keep the level from being decremented
    if they are declared right after each other.
    
    Fixes #157.

M	lizard_languages/clike.py
M	test/testNestedStructures.py

commit 497051b74cc4b2655a59177d89232fc73ada6cb7
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Dec 30 08:41:36 2016 -0800

    Fix `nesting_level` for brace-less ctrl structures
    
    The nesting structure extension
    is running before the assignment of the nesting level for tokens.
    The solution is to increment the nesting level
    right at the end of control-flow structure declaration
    but before its body.
    
    In addition,
    the token is yielded before being processed
    to simulate running the extension after the code reader,
    but this is somewhat hacky.
    
    This bug (surprisingly) has been a feature!
    The fix breaks the gotcha braceless nested if-then-else structures.
    The current implementation of the metric looks wrong overall.
    
    Fixes #157.

M	lizard_ext/lizardns.py
M	lizard_languages/clike.py

commit d82a52f1ba33c17ea48d2a7992b1cafd1c1b699c
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Dec 30 08:41:56 2016 -0800

    Add tests for braceless consecutive structures
    
    The tests expose a bug of overcounting of nested structures
    with consecutive brace-less (single statement) control flow structures.
    
    Add tests for nested braceless ctrl flow structures
    
    Issue #157.

commit a8fd8674b6070ff436cefda4f3eefb0ffda01f61
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Aug 29 04:41:49 2016 -0700

    Add a test for Nvidia CUDA dialect <<< and >>>
    
    The current implementation in Lizard
    doesn't recognize these special tokens.
    However, the use cases do not affect the complexity metrics,
    which is more important than accurate token count.
    
    Originally, Lizard recognized '>>>' token,
    but it broke C++11 template code as in PR #68.
    The current strategy of ignoring these dialect tokens
    seems to be good enough.

commit 5e6fe3ed07dd23ddf85f3a833cb83270a7190912
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jun 7 15:43:59 2016 -0700

    Ignore template parameters
    
    Template parameters are not currently considered in any analyses.
    The 'class' keyword in template parameters is messing
    other Lizard states' assumptions.
    
    If anyone wants to do complexity analysis of
    C++ templates, meta-programming,
    this could be a good start.

commit be8e434eae269c5c6fe4f59ecb8ff895fada3926
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu May 5 00:14:13 2016 -0700

    Ignore terminators within parentheses in NS count
    
    The code within parentheses is ignored upon counting nested structures.
    Fore example:
    
        for (int a;;) if (b) return c;
    
    The ';' within the parentheses terminates structure detection
    if not ignored.
    The implementation would guess
    that this is a "for" loop without braces.

M	lizard_ext/lizardns.py
M	test/testNestedStructures.py

    Add Nested Structure counts into thresholds
    
    This addition properly generates warnings for code
    exceeding the maximum number of nested control structures.

commit 9b17f39012fba4f19a1bd55af45782ae9b96c313
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed May 4 22:39:38 2016 -0700

    Implement counting of Nested Control Structures
    
    The tests and implementation are borrowed from the Nesting Depth code;
    however, the counting of the nested control structures
    is implemented with stack for simplicity,
    which can be inefficient (worth measuring!).
    
    Note that this implementation does not provide
    user facing front-end controls to generate warnings.
    It only prints the metric in the summary page.
    
    The implementation is only for C-like languages
    with C++ being the main target.
    
    The implementation is only tested with simple code snippets
    and not verified against production code.

A	lizard_ext/lizardns.py
M	lizard_languages/code_reader.py
A	test/testNestedStructures.py

Merge: 3ff25a8 5fe588b

    Merge pull request #93 from rakhimov/division
    
    Use Python3 division for calculation of averages

commit 5fe588bee97b36e991c7a18a6df8bdecc3be9ea0
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 9 10:00:30 2016 -0800

    Use Python3 division for calculation of averages
    
    In some places, it seems that the results of calculations
    are expected to be floats,
    but integer division of Python2 is used.
    In other places, explicit cast to float is made to get the float result.
    Python3 division approach for integers helps cleanup these places
    and make them consistent.
    
    If Lizard relies on integer division approach of Python2,
    which doesn't seem to be the case,
    the code must be corrected with '//'.

M	lizard.py

commit a0c9ef8f1507de755ccf8c042b0550225745378b
Merge: 16c0c8c 9fd9cda
Author: Terry Yin <terry.yinzhe@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jan 9 14:26:21 2016 +0800

    Merge pull request #79 from rakhimov/exclude-assert
    
    Exclude code in C/C++ 'assert' from CCN

commit 9fd9cdaefe89270d45b182de84863c6b54e4f31e
Author: rakhimov <ol.rakhimov@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jan 8 04:31:09 2016 -0800

    Exclude code in C/C++ 'assert' from CCN
    
    Consider a simple use case:
    
    assert((conditional_expression) && "More description...");
    
    This line adds 1 + CCN(conditional_expression)
    if the assertion is counted as a part of a function.
    
    Since assertions are mostly used
    to check (pre, post)-conditions,
    to explicitly state assumptions,
    and to catch programmer errors,
    they are not expected to be a part of the flow of a function.
    Moreover, assertions with side-effects is a very bad idea.
    The function should stay the same
    if all the assertions are removed (in release mode, for example).

M	lizard.py
M	test/testCyclomaticComplexity.py

commit f62eaf7a98032e9ed2222cade41c353f001a5cbc
Merge: 7979ffe 9aa8b4e
Author: Terry Yin <terry.yinzhe@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Feb 2 22:43:33 2014 -0800

    Merge pull request #30 from jannero/master
    
    Calculate Modified CCN

commit 9aa8b4e3cebfab8b99cfc950e4663e4c66593585
Author: Janne Rönkkö <janne.ronkko@vincit.fi>
Date:   Mon Feb 3 07:32:34 2014 +0200

    Add support for calculating modified CCN
    
    In modified CCN multi-decision structure is considered as single
    unit, i.e. each decision in such structure is not counted. Instead
    the whole structure increases CCN by 1. For example, consider
    the following code:
    
    switch(value)
    {
        case V1: break;
        case V2: break;
    }
    
    When using modified CCN the calculated value is 2 but with normal
    CCN the value is 3.

M	lizard.py
M	test/testApplication.py

commit d941ac62a26e4f73d036a4b0deef8e83b3a4df1b
Author: Janne Rönkkö <janne.ronkko@vincit.fi>
Date:   Mon Feb 3 07:53:38 2014 +0200

    Refactor option passing to language readers
    
    By passing the options in the __init__ function for the
    LanguageRearedBase object it is easier to add new options that affect
    the behaviour of the language reader.
    
    The change makes adding configurability to LanguageChooser easier as
    the used LanguageChooser object is instantiated only in one place.

M	lizard.py

Author: Daniel Jackson <e28eta@yahoo.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 27 16:30:10 2013 -0800

    Option to print warnings in clang's format
    
    This makes it easier to integrate hfcca.py into an existing build that already knows
    how to parse and display warnings from clang/gcc.
    
    For example, Xcode. Add a Run Script build phase that runs hfcca.py, and any methods that
    exceed the complexity will be flagged.
